   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Chad</h1>

    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Landlocked country in northern central Africa
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the country. For the given name, see <a href="/wiki/Chad_(name)" title="Chad (name)">Chad (name)</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Chad_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Chad (disambiguation)">Chad (disambiguation)</a>.

         <td>1.9</td>
        </tr>

      <p><b>Chad</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/tʃ/: 'ch' in 'China'">tʃ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Chad.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/En-us-Chad.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Chad.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">تشاد</span>‎ <i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Tšād</i>, <small>Arabic pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic" title="Help:IPA/Arabic">[tʃaːd]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Tchad</i>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[tʃa(d)]</a></span>), officially known as the <b>Republic of Chad</b> (Arabic: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">جمهورية&nbsp;تْشَاد</span>‎ <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Jumhūriyyat Tšād</i></i>; French: <i lang="fr">République du Tchad</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">north</a>-<a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">central Africa</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chad%E2%80%93Libya_border" title="Chad–Libya border">the north</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chad%E2%80%93Sudan_border" title="Chad–Sudan border">the east</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic%E2%80%93Chad_border" title="Central African Republic–Chad border">the south</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cameroon%E2%80%93Chad_border" title="Cameroon–Chad border">the south-west</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chad%E2%80%93Nigeria_border" title="Chad–Nigeria border">the southwest</a> (at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chad%E2%80%93Niger_border" title="Chad–Niger border">the west</a>. </p>
      <p>Chad has several regions: a <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> zone in the north, an arid <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian</a> belt in the centre and a more fertile <a href="/wiki/Sudanian_Savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudanian Savanna">Sudanian Savanna</a> zone in the south. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>, after which the country is named, is the largest <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetland</a> in Chad and the second-largest in Africa. The capital <a href="/wiki/N%27Djamena" title="N'Djamena">N'Djamena</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Chad" title="List of cities in Chad">city</a>. Chad's official languages are <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. Chad is home to over 200 different <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_in_Chad" title="List of ethnic groups in Chad">ethnic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Chad" title="Languages of Chad">linguistic groups</a>. <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Chad" title="Islam in Chad">Islam</a> (51.8%) and <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Chad" title="Christianity in Chad">Christianity</a> (44.1%) are the main <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Chad" title="Religion in Chad">religions practiced in Chad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Beginning in the 7th millennium BC, human populations moved into the Chadian basin in great numbers. By the end of the 1st millennium AD, a series of states and empires had risen and fallen in Chad's Sahelian strip, each focused on controlling the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> routes that passed through the region. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> conquered the territory by 1920 and incorporated it as part of <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a>. In 1960, Chad obtained independence under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Tombalbaye" title="François Tombalbaye">François Tombalbaye</a>. Resentment towards his policies in the Muslim north culminated in the eruption of a long-lasting <a href="/wiki/The_Tombalbaye_Regime#Rebellion_in_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="The Tombalbaye Regime">civil war</a> in 1965. In 1979 <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Government_of_National_Unity" title="Transitional Government of National Unity">the rebels</a> conquered the capital and put an end to the South's hegemony. But, the rebel commanders fought amongst themselves until <a href="/wiki/Hiss%C3%A8ne_Habr%C3%A9" title="Hissène Habré">Hissène Habré</a> defeated his rivals. <a href="/wiki/Chadian%E2%80%93Libyan_conflict" title="Chadian–Libyan conflict">Chadian–Libyan conflict</a> erupted in 1978 by the Libyan invasion which stopped in 1987 with a French military intervention (<a href="/wiki/Operation_%C3%89pervier" title="Operation Épervier">Operation Épervier</a>). Hissène Habré was overthrown in turn in 1990 by his general <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a>. With French support, a modernization of the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Chad" title="Military of Chad">Chadian armed forces</a> was initiated in 1991. Since 2003 the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Darfur" title="War in Darfur">Darfur crisis</a> in Sudan has spilt over the border and <a href="/wiki/Chadian_Civil_War_(2005%E2%80%932010)" title="Chadian Civil War (2005–2010)">destabilised the nation</a>. Poor already, the nation and people struggled to accommodate the hundreds of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudanese refugees">Sudanese refugees</a> who live in and around camps in eastern Chad. </p>
      <p>While many political parties are active, power lies firmly in the hands of President Déby and his political party, the <a href="/wiki/Patriotic_Salvation_Movement" title="Patriotic Salvation Movement">Patriotic Salvation Movement</a>. Chad remains plagued by <a href="/wiki/Political_violence" title="Political violence">political violence</a> and recurrent attempted <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coups d'état</a>. Chad is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">poorest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">most corrupt</a> countries in the world; most inhabitants live in poverty as <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Chad" title="Agriculture in Chad">subsistence herders and farmers</a>. Since 2003 <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">crude oil</a> has become the country's primary source of export earnings, superseding the traditional <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> industry. Chad has a poor <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Chad" title="Human rights in Chad">human rights record</a>, with frequent abuses such as arbitrary imprisonment, extrajudicial killings, and limits on civil liberties by both security forces and armed militias. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Chad" title="History of Chad">History of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 7th millennium BCE, ecological conditions in the northern half of Chadian territory favored human settlement, and its population increased considerably. Some of the most important <a href="/wiki/African_archaeology" title="African archaeology">African archaeological</a> sites are found in Chad, mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region">Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region</a>; some date to earlier than 2000 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg/220px-Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg/330px-Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg/440px-Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3496" data-file-height="2416"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Kanem-Bu_warriors.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Group of Kanem-Bu warriors. The <a href="/wiki/Kanem-Bornu_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanem-Bornu Empire">Kanem-Bornu Empire</a> controlled almost all of what is today Chad.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>For more than 2,000 years, the Chadian Basin has been inhabited by agricultural and <a href="/wiki/Sedentism" title="Sedentism">sedentary</a> people. The region became a crossroads of civilizations. The earliest of these were the legendary <a href="/wiki/Sao_civilisation" title="Sao civilisation">Sao</a>, known from artifacts and oral histories. The Sao fell to the <a href="/wiki/Kanem_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanem Empire">Kanem Empire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lange88_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lange88-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> the first and longest-lasting of the empires that developed in Chad's <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian</a> strip by the end of the 1st millennium AD. Two other states in the region, <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Bagirmi" title="Sultanate of Bagirmi">Sultanate of Bagirmi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wadai_Empire" title="Wadai Empire">Wadai Empire</a> emerged in the 16th and 17th centuries. The power of Kanem and its successors was based on control of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> routes that passed through the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup> These states, at least tacitly <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Africa" title="Islam in Africa">Muslim</a>, never extended their control to the southern grasslands except to raid for slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In Kanem, about a third of the population were slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg/220px-Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg/330px-Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg/440px-Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3286" data-file-height="2836"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_soldier_of_WWII.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Chadian soldier fighting for <a href="/wiki/Free_French_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Free French Forces">Free France</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The Free French Forces included 15,000 soldiers from Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>French colonial expansion led to the creation of the <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Territoire Militaire des Pays et Protectorats du Tchad</i> in 1900. By 1920, France had secured full control of the colony and incorporated it as part of <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial Chad">French rule in Chad</a> was characterised by an absence of policies to unify the territory and sluggish modernisation compared to other French colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-Decalo,_pp._8–9_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decalo,_pp._8–9-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French primarily viewed the colony as an unimportant source of untrained labour and raw cotton; France introduced large-scale cotton production in 1929. The colonial administration in Chad was critically understaffed and had to rely on the dregs of the French civil service. Only the <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a> of the south was governed effectively; French presence in the Islamic north and east was nominal. The educational system was affected by this neglect.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Decalo,_pp._8–9_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Decalo,_pp._8–9-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, France granted Chad the status of <a href="/wiki/Overseas_France" title="Overseas France">overseas territory</a> and its inhabitants the right to elect representatives to the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(France)" title="National Assembly (France)">National Assembly</a> and a <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Chad)" title="National Assembly (Chad)">Chadian assembly</a>. The largest political party was the <a href="/wiki/Chadian_Progressive_Party" title="Chadian Progressive Party">Chadian Progressive Party</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Parti Progressiste Tchadien</i>, PPT), based in the southern half of the colony. Chad was granted independence on 11 August 1960 with the PPT's leader, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Tombalbaye" title="François Tombalbaye">François Tombalbaye</a>, an ethnic <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a>, as its first <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state_of_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of state of Chad">president</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Two years later, Tombalbaye banned opposition parties and established a one-party system. Tombalbaye's autocratic rule and insensitive mismanagement exacerbated inter-ethnic tensions. In 1965, Muslims in the north, led by the <a href="/wiki/FROLINAT" title="FROLINAT">National Liberation Front of Chad</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Front de libération nationale du Tchad</i>, FRONILAT), began a <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Government_of_National_Unity" title="Transitional Government of National Unity">civil war</a>. Tombalbaye was <a href="/wiki/1975_Chadian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1975 Chadian coup d'état">overthrown and killed</a> in 1975,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> but the insurgency continued. In 1979 the rebel factions led by <a href="/wiki/Hiss%C3%A8ne_Habr%C3%A9" title="Hissène Habré">Hissène Habré</a> took the capital, and all central authority in the country collapsed. Armed factions, many from the north's rebellion, contended for power.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The disintegration of Chad caused the collapse of France's position in the country. <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> moved to fill the power vacuum and became <a href="/wiki/Chadian-Libyan_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Chadian-Libyan conflict">involved in Chad's civil war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Libya's adventure <a href="/wiki/Toyota_War" title="Toyota War">ended in disaster</a> in 1987; the French-supported president, <a href="/wiki/Hiss%C3%A8ne_Habr%C3%A9" title="Hissène Habré">Hissène Habré</a>, evoked a united response from Chadians of a kind never seen before<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and forced the Libyan army off Chadian soil.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Habré consolidated his dictatorship through a power system that relied on corruption and violence with thousands of people estimated to have been killed under his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The president favoured his own <a href="/wiki/Toubou_people" title="Toubou people">Toubou</a> ethnic group and discriminated against his former allies, the <a href="/wiki/Zaghawa_people" title="Zaghawa people">Zaghawa</a>. His general, <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a>, overthrew him in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Attempts to prosecute Habré led to his placement under house arrest in <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> in 2005; in 2013, Habré was formally charged with war crimes committed during his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In May 2016, he was found guilty of human-rights abuses, including rape, sexual slavery, and ordering the killing of 40,000 people, and sentenced to life in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_(cropped)2014.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png/220px-Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png/330px-Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_%28cropped%292014.png 2x" data-file-width="405" data-file-height="439"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Idriss_Deby_with_Obamas_(cropped)2014.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Despite internal political opposition, coup attempts, and a civil war, <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a> has continuously ruled Chad since 1990.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Déby attempted to reconcile the rebel groups and reintroduced multiparty politics. Chadians approved a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Chad" title="Constitution of Chad">new constitution</a> by <a href="/wiki/Chadian_constitutional_referendum,_1996" class="mw-redirect" title="Chadian constitutional referendum, 1996">referendum</a>, and in 1996, Déby easily won a <a href="/wiki/Chadian_presidential_election,_1996" class="mw-redirect" title="Chadian presidential election, 1996">competitive presidential election</a>. He won a <a href="/wiki/Chadian_presidential_election,_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="Chadian presidential election, 2001">second term</a> five years later.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil</a> exploitation began in Chad in 2003, bringing with it hopes that Chad would, at last, have some chances of peace and prosperity. Instead, internal dissent worsened, and a <a href="/wiki/War_in_Chad_(2005%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Chad (2005–present)">new civil war</a> broke out. Déby <a href="/wiki/Chadian_constitutional_referendum,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Chadian constitutional referendum, 2005">unilaterally modified the constitution</a> to remove the two-term limit on the presidency; this caused an uproar among the civil society and opposition parties.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006 Déby won <a href="/wiki/Chadian_presidential_election,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Chadian presidential election, 2006">a third mandate</a> in elections that the opposition boycotted. Ethnic violence in eastern Chad has increased; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> has warned that a <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> like that in <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur</a> may yet occur in Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2006)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2006)">In 2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2008)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2008)">in 2008</a> rebel forces attempted to take the capital by force, but failed on both occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> An agreement for the restoration of harmony between Chad and Sudan, signed 15 January 2010, marked the end of a five-year war.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The fix in relations led to the Chadian rebels from Sudan returning home, the opening of the border between the two countries after seven years of closure, and the deployment of a joint force to secure the border. In May 2013, security forces in Chad foiled a coup against President <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a> that had been in preparation for several months.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chad is currently one of the leading partners in a <a href="/wiki/Multinational_Joint_Task_Force" title="Multinational Joint Task Force">West African coalition</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Boko_Haram_insurgency" title="Boko Haram insurgency">fight</a> against <a href="/wiki/Boko_Haram" title="Boko Haram">Boko Haram</a>. Chad has also been included on Presidential Proclamation 9645, the expanded version of United States president <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump's</a> <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_13780" title="Executive Order 13780">Executive Order 13780</a>, which restricts entry by nationals from 8 countries, including Chad, into the US. This move has angered the Chadian government.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span id="Geography.2C_climate_and_environment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography,_climate_and_environment">Geography, climate and environment</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Chad" title="Geography of Chad">Geography of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chad_sat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Chad_sat.jpg/170px-Chad_sat.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Chad_sat.jpg/255px-Chad_sat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Chad_sat.jpg/340px-Chad_sat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1265" data-file-height="1922"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chad_sat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Chad is divided into three distinct zones, the <a href="/wiki/Sudanian_Savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudanian Savanna">Sudanian Savanna</a> in the south, the <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahara Desert">Sahara Desert</a> in the north, and the <a href="/wiki/Sahelian" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian">Sahelian</a> belt in the center.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg/220px-ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg/330px-ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg/440px-ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="566"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ShrinkingLakeChad-1973-1997-EO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> in a 2001 satellite image. On the top, the changes from 1973 to 1997 are shown, with the lake shrinking.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 1,284,000 square kilometres (496,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-area_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-area-2">[2]</a></sup> Chad is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">20th-largest country</a>. It is slightly smaller than <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and slightly larger than South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Chad is in north central Africa, lying between latitudes <a href="/wiki/7th_parallel_north" title="7th parallel north">7°</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_parallel_north" title="24th parallel north">24°N</a>, and <a href="/wiki/13th_meridian_east" title="13th meridian east">13°</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_meridian_east" title="24th meridian east">24°E</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg/220px-Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg/330px-Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg/440px-Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ounianga_Lakes_from_ISS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>This astronaut photograph features one of the largest of a series of ten mostly fresh water lakes in the Ounianga Basin in the heart of the Sahara Desert of northeastern Chad.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad is bounded to the north by <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, to the east by <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, to the west by <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, and to the south by the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>. The country's capital is 1,060 kilometres (660&nbsp;mi) from the nearest seaport, <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>, Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-41">[41]</a></sup> Because of this distance from the sea and the country's largely <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> climate, Chad is sometimes referred to as the "Dead Heart of Africa".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The dominant physical structure is a wide basin bounded to the north and east by the <a href="/wiki/Ennedi_Plateau" title="Ennedi Plateau">Ennedi Plateau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibesti_Mountains" title="Tibesti Mountains">Tibesti Mountains</a>, which include <a href="/wiki/Emi_Koussi" title="Emi Koussi">Emi Koussi</a>, a dormant <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> that reaches 3,414 metres (11,201&nbsp;ft) above sea level. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>, after which the country is named (and which in turn takes its name from the <a href="/wiki/Kanuri_language" title="Kanuri language">Kanuri</a> word for "lake"<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>), is the remains of an immense lake that occupied 330,000 square kilometres (130,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of the <a href="/wiki/Chad_Basin" title="Chad Basin">Chad Basin</a> 7,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup> Although in the 21st century it covers only 17,806 square kilometres (6,875&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and its surface area is subject to heavy seasonal fluctuations,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> the lake is Africa's second largest wetland.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chad is home to six terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna">East Sudanian savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_Acacia_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian Acacia savanna">Sahelian Acacia savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad_flooded_savanna" title="Lake Chad flooded savanna">Lake Chad flooded savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Saharan_montane_xeric_woodlands" title="East Saharan montane xeric woodlands">East Saharan montane xeric woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Saharan_steppe_and_woodlands" title="South Saharan steppe and woodlands">South Saharan steppe and woodlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tibesti-Jebel_Uweinat_montane_xeric_woodlands" title="Tibesti-Jebel Uweinat montane xeric woodlands">Tibesti-Jebel Uweinat montane xeric woodlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-46">[46]</a></sup> The region's tall grasses and extensive marshes make it favourable for birds, reptiles, and large mammals. Chad's major rivers—the <a href="/wiki/Chari_River" title="Chari River">Chari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logone_River" title="Logone River">Logone</a> and their tributaries—flow through the southern savannas from the southeast into Lake Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Chad">Climate of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Each year a tropical weather system known as the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">intertropical front</a> crosses Chad from south to north, bringing a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> that lasts from May to October in the south, and from June to September in the Sahel.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Variations in local rainfall create three major geographical zones. The <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> lies in the country's northern third. Yearly precipitations throughout this belt are under 50 millimetres (2.0&nbsp;in); only occasional spontaneous palm groves survive, all of them south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Sahara gives way to a <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelian</a> belt in Chad's centre; precipitation there varies from 300 to 600&nbsp;mm (11.8 to 23.6&nbsp;in) per year. In the Sahel, a steppe of thorny bushes (mostly <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacias</a>) gradually gives way to the south to <a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna">East Sudanian savanna</a> in Chad's <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudanese</a> zone. Yearly rainfall in this belt is over 900&nbsp;mm (35.4&nbsp;in).<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Chad" title="Wildlife of Chad">Wildlife of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg/220px-African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg/330px-African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg/440px-African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1044"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:African_Bush_Elephant_Mikumi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/African_bush_elephant" title="African bush elephant">African bush elephant</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad's animal and plant life correspond to the three climatic zones. In the Saharan region, the only flora is the date-palm groves of the oasis. Palms and <a href="/wiki/Acacia_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Acacia tree">acacia trees</a> grow in the Sahelian region. The southern, or Sudanic, zone consists of broad grasslands or prairies suitable for grazing. As of 2002, there were at least 134 species of mammals, 509 species of birds (354 species of residents and 155 migrants), and over 1,600 species of plants throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Flora_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flora-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">Elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_buffalo" title="African buffalo">buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus">hippopotamuses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceroses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giraffe" title="Giraffe">giraffes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheetah" title="Cheetah">cheetahs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyena" title="Hyena">hyenas</a>, and many species of <a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">snakes</a> are found here, although most large carnivore populations have been drastically reduced since the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LTQ_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LTQ-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elephant_hunting_in_Chad" title="Elephant hunting in Chad">Elephant poaching</a>, particularly in the south of the country in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Zakouma_National_Park" title="Zakouma National Park">Zakouma National Park</a>, is a severe problem. The small group of surviving <a href="/wiki/West_African_crocodile" title="West African crocodile">West African crocodiles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ennedi_Plateau" title="Ennedi Plateau">Ennedi Plateau</a> represents one of the last colonies known in the Sahara today.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Extensive deforestation has resulted in loss of trees such as acacias, baobab, dates and palm trees. Chad had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.18/10, ranking it 83<sup>rd</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-53">[53]</a></sup> This has also caused loss of natural habitat for wild animals; one of the main reasons for this is also hunting and livestock farming by increasing human settlements. Populations of animals like lions, leopards and rhino have fallen significantly.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Efforts have been made by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> to improve relations between farmers, agro-pastoralists and pastoralists in the Zakouma National Park (ZNP), Siniaka-Minia, and Aouk reserve in southeastern Chad to promote sustainable development.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> As part of the national conservation effort, more than 1.2&nbsp;million trees have been replanted to check the advancement of the desert, which incidentally also helps the local economy by way of financial return from acacia trees, which produce <a href="/wiki/Gum_arabic" title="Gum arabic">gum arabic</a>, and also from fruit trees.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Poaching is a serious problem in the country, particularly of elephants for the profitable <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a> industry and a threat to lives of rangers even in the national parks such as Zakouma. Elephants are often massacred in herds in and around the parks by organized poaching.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The problem is worsened by the fact that the parks are understaffed and that a number of wardens have been murdered by poachers.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Chad" title="Demographics of Chad">Demographics of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <caption>
        Population in Chad<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-59">[59]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th scope="col">Year </th> 
         <th scope="col">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">2.5 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">8.3 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">15.5 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Chad's national statistical agency projected the country's 2015 population between 13,630,252 and 13,679,203, with 13,670,084 as its medium projection; based on the medium projection, 3,212,470 people lived in urban areas and 10,457,614 people lived in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-INSEEDproj_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INSEEDproj-3">[3]</a></sup> The country's population is young: an estimated 47.3% is under 15. The birth rate is estimated at 42.35 births per 1,000 people, the mortality rate at 16.69. The life expectancy is 52 years.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:180px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ouaddaian_girl_from_Chad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/Ouaddaian_girl_from_Chad.jpg" decoding="async" width="178" height="197" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="178" data-file-height="197"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ouaddaian_girl_from_Chad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/Ouadda%C3%AF_Region" title="Ouaddaï Region">Ouaddaian</a> girl
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad's population is unevenly distributed. Density is 0.1/km<sup>2</sup> (0.26/sq&nbsp;mi) in the Saharan <a href="/wiki/Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region">Borkou-Ennedi-Tibesti Region</a> but 52.4/km<sup>2</sup> (136/sq&nbsp;mi) in the <a href="/wiki/Logone_Occidental_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Logone Occidental Region">Logone Occidental Region</a>. In the capital, it is even higher.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCHR_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCHR-41">[41]</a></sup> About half of the nation's population lives in the southern fifth of its territory, making this the most densely populated region.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Urban life is concentrated in the capital, whose population is mostly engaged in commerce. The other major towns are <a href="/wiki/Sarh" title="Sarh">Sarh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moundou" title="Moundou">Moundou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ab%C3%A9ch%C3%A9" title="Abéché">Abéché</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doba,_Chad" title="Doba, Chad">Doba</a>, which are considerably smaller but growing rapidly in population and economic activity.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup> Since 2003, 230,000 <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_refugees_in_Chad" title="Sudanese refugees in Chad">Sudanese refugees</a> have fled to eastern Chad from war-ridden Darfur. With the 172,600 Chadians displaced by the civil war in the east, this has generated increased tensions among the region's communities.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">Polygamy</a> is common, with 39% of women living in such unions. This is sanctioned by law, which automatically permits polygamy unless spouses specify that this is unacceptable upon marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Although violence against women is prohibited, domestic violence is common. <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_cutting" class="mw-redirect" title="Female genital cutting">Female genital mutilation</a> is also prohibited, but the practice is widespread and deeply rooted in tradition; 45% of Chadian women undergo the procedure, with the highest rates among <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hadjarai" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadjarai">Hadjarai</a>, and Ouaddaians (90% or more). Lower percentages were reported among the <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a> (38%) and the <a href="/wiki/Toubou" class="mw-redirect" title="Toubou">Toubou</a> (2%). Women lack equal opportunities in education and training, making it difficult for them to compete for the relatively few formal-sector jobs. Although property and inheritance laws based on the French code do not discriminate against women, local leaders adjudicate most inheritance cases in favour of men, according to traditional practice.<sup id="cite_ref-HRP_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRP-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3> 
      <p>The peoples of Chad carry significant ancestry from <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">Eastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">Western</a>, and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">Northern Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chad has more than 200 distinct ethnic groups,<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup> which create diverse social structures. The colonial administration and independent governments have attempted to impose a national society, but for most Chadians the local or regional society remains the most important influence outside the immediate family. Nevertheless, Chad's people may be classified according to the geographical region in which they live.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the south live sedentary people such as the <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a>, the nation's main ethnic group, whose essential <a href="/wiki/Social_unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Social unit">social unit</a> is the lineage. In the Sahel sedentary peoples live side by side with nomadic ones, such as the Arabs, the country's second major ethnic group. The north is inhabited by nomads, mostly <a href="/wiki/Toubous" class="mw-redirect" title="Toubous">Toubous</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Chad" title="Languages of Chad">Languages of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad's official languages are <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, but over 100 languages and dialects are spoken. Due to the important role played by itinerant Arab traders and settled merchants in local communities, <a href="/wiki/Chadian_Arabic" title="Chadian Arabic">Chadian Arabic</a> has become a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Chad" title="Religion in Chad">Religion in Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad is a religiously diverse country. Various estimates, including from Pew Research Center in 2010, found that 51.8 - 57.7% of the population was Muslim, while 39% - 44.1% were Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> 21.5% were Catholic and a further 16.6% were Protestant.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Christians_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Christians-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Muslims_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Muslims-71">[71]</a></sup> Among Muslims, 48% professed to be <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>, 21% <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a>, 4% <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadi</a> and 23% <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim" title="Non-denominational Muslim">just Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pew128_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew128-72">[72]</a></sup> A small proportion of the population continues to practice indigenous religions. Animism includes a variety of ancestor and place-oriented religions whose expression is highly specific. Islam is expressed in diverse ways; for example, 55% of Muslim Chadians belong to <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> <a href="/wiki/Tariqa" title="Tariqa">orders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pew128_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew128-72">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Africa" title="Christianity in Africa">Christianity</a> arrived in Chad with the French and American missionaries; as with Chadian Islam, it <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretises</a> aspects of pre-Christian religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup> Muslims are largely concentrated in northern and eastern Chad, and animists and Christians live primarily in southern Chad and <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A9ra_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Guéra Region">Guéra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup> The constitution provides for a secular state and guarantees religious freedom; different religious communities generally co-exist without problems.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">

          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">religion</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">percent</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Chad" title="Islam in Chad">Islam</a></td>

            <div style="background:blue; width:39%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td>

           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">Folk</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
