          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Chad" title="Freedom of religion in Chad">Other</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:gray; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of Muslims in the country are adherents of a moderate branch of mystical Islam (<a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>). Its most common expression is the <a href="/wiki/Tijaniyah" class="mw-redirect" title="Tijaniyah">Tijaniyah</a>, an order followed by the 35% of Chadian Muslims which incorporates some local African religious elements.<sup id="cite_ref-pew128_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew128-72">[72]</a></sup> A small minority of the country's Muslims hold more fundamentalist practices, which, in some cases, may be associated with Saudi-oriented <a href="/wiki/Salafi_movement" title="Salafi movement">Salafi movements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> represent the largest Christian denomination in the country. Most Protestants, including the Nigeria-based "Winners' Chapel", are affiliated with various evangelical Christian groups. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> religious communities also are present in the country. Both faiths were introduced after independence in 1960 and therefore are considered to be "new" religions in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chad is home to foreign missionaries representing both <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> and Islamic groups. Itinerant <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> preachers, primarily from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, also visit. Saudi Arabian funding generally supports social and educational projects and extensive mosque construction.<sup id="cite_ref-US-DoS-IRFR-2006_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US-DoS-IRFR-2006-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Chad" title="Politics of Chad">Politics of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad's constitution provides for a strong executive branch headed by a president who dominates the political system. The president has the power to appoint the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Chad">prime minister</a> and the cabinet, and exercises considerable influence over appointments of judges, generals, provincial officials and heads of Chad's para-statal firms.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In cases of grave and immediate threat, the president, in consultation with the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Chad)" title="National Assembly (Chad)">National Assembly</a>, may declare a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>. The president is <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Chad" title="Elections in Chad">directly elected</a> by popular vote for a five-year term; in 2005 constitutional term limits were removed,<sup id="cite_ref-Term2_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Term2-76">[76]</a></sup> allowing a president to remain in power beyond the previous two-term limit.<sup id="cite_ref-Term2_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Term2-76">[76]</a></sup> Most of Déby's key advisers are members of the Zaghawa ethnic group, although southern and opposition personalities are represented in <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Chad" title="Government of Chad">government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNPACP_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPACP-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chad's legal system is based on <a href="/wiki/Law_of_France" title="Law of France">French civil law</a> and Chadian customary law where the latter does not interfere with public order or constitutional guarantees of equality. Despite the constitution's guarantee of judicial independence, the president names most key judicial officials. The legal system's highest jurisdictions, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Chad" title="Supreme Court of Chad">Supreme Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Council_of_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional Council of Chad">Constitutional Council</a>, have become fully operational since 2000. The Supreme Court is made up of a chief justice, named by the president, and 15 councillors, appointed for life by the president and the National Assembly. The Constitutional Court is headed by nine judges elected to nine-year terms. It has the power to review legislation, treaties and international agreements prior to their adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNPACP_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNPACP-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The National Assembly makes legislation. The body consists of 155 members elected for four-year terms who meet three times per year. The Assembly holds regular sessions twice a year, starting in March and October, and can hold special sessions when called by the prime minister. Deputies elect a National Assembly president every two years. The president must sign or reject newly passed laws within 15 days. The National Assembly must approve the prime minister's plan of government and may force the prime minister to resign through a majority vote of no confidence. However, if the National Assembly rejects the executive branch's programme twice in one year, the president may disband the Assembly and call for new legislative elections. In practice, the president exercises considerable influence over the National Assembly through his party, the <a href="/wiki/Patriotic_Salvation_Movement" title="Patriotic Salvation Movement">Patriotic Salvation Movement</a> (MPS), which holds a large majority.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until the legalisation of opposition parties in 1992, Déby's MPS was the sole legal party in Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup> Since then, <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Chad" title="List of political parties in Chad">78 registered political parties</a> have become active.<sup id="cite_ref-HRP_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRP-65">[65]</a></sup> In 2005, opposition parties and human rights organisations supported the boycott of the constitutional referendum that allowed Déby to stand for re-election for a third term<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> amid reports of widespread irregularities in voter registration and government censorship of independent media outlets during the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-79">[79]</a></sup> Correspondents judged the 2006 presidential elections a mere formality, as the opposition deemed the polls a farce and boycotted them.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chad is listed as a <a href="/wiki/Failed_state" title="Failed state">failed state</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Fund_for_Peace" title="Fund for Peace">Fund for Peace</a> (FFP). In 2007 Chad had the seventh highest score on the failed state index. Since then the trend has been upwards each year. Chad had the fourth highest score (behind Sudan) on the Failed State Index of 2012 and as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, is ranked fifth.<sup id="cite_ref-fundforpeace.org_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fundforpeace.org-81">[81]</a></sup> Corruption is rife at all levels; <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> for 2005 named Chad (tied with <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>) as the most corrupt country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Chad's ranking on the index has improved only marginally in recent years. Since its first inclusion on the index in 2004, Chad's best score has been 2/10 for 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Critics of President Déby have accused him of <a href="/wiki/Cronyism" title="Cronyism">cronyism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tribalism" title="Tribalism">tribalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tribe_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tribe-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In southern Chad, bitter conflicts over land are becoming more and more common. They frequently turn violent. Long-standing community culture is being eroded – and so are the livelihoods of many farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-D+C_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D+C-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Chad" title="LGBT rights in Chad">Homosexual acts</a> are illegal and can be punished by 15 to 20 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In December 2016, Chad passed a law criminalising both male and female same-sex sexual activity by a vote of 111 to 1.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_opposition_and_foreign_relations">Internal opposition and foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Chad" title="Foreign relations of Chad">Foreign relations of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Chad_(Washington,_D.C.).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG/220px-Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG/330px-Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG/440px-Embassy_of_Chad_%28Washington%2C_D.C.%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1976" data-file-height="1712"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Chad_(Washington,_D.C.).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Chad_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Embassy of Chad in Washington, D.C.">Embassy of Chad in Washington, D.C.</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Déby faces armed opposition from groups who are deeply divided by leadership clashes but united in their intention to overthrow him.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> These forces <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2006)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2006)">stormed the capital</a> on 13 April 2006, but were ultimately repelled. Chad's greatest foreign influence is France, which maintains 1,000 soldiers in the country. Déby relies on the French to help repel the rebels, and France gives the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Chad" title="Military of Chad">Chadian army</a> logistical and intelligence support for fear of a complete collapse of regional stability.<sup id="cite_ref-PINR_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PINR-89">[89]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Franco-Chadian relations were soured by the granting of oil drilling rights to the American <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">Exxon</a> company in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There have been numerous rebel groups in Chad throughout the last few decades. In 2007, a peace treaty was signed that integrated <a href="/wiki/United_Front_for_Democratic_Change" title="United Front for Democratic Change">United Front for Democratic Change</a> or <b>FUC</b> soldiers into the Chadian Army.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Justice_and_Democracy_in_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Movement for Justice and Democracy in Chad">Movement for Justice and Democracy in Chad</a> or <b>MDJT</b> also clashed with government forces in 2003 in an attempt to overthrow President <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a>. In addition, there have been various conflicts with <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a> rebels in eastern Chad, who killed civilians by use of <a href="/wiki/Helicopter_gunship" class="mw-redirect" title="Helicopter gunship">helicopter gunships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Presently, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Resistance_Forces" title="Union of Resistance Forces">Union of Resistance Forces</a> or <b>UFR</b> are a rebel group that continues to battle with the government of Chad. In 2010, the UFR reportedly had a force estimating 6,000 men and 300 vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Chad" title="Regions of Chad">Regions of Chad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Chad" title="Departments of Chad">Departments of Chad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sub-prefectures_of_Chad" title="Sub-prefectures of Chad">Sub-prefectures of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2012 Chad has been divided into <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Chad" title="Regions of Chad">23 regions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-statoids_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statoids-94">[94]</a></sup> The subdivision of Chad in regions came about in 2003 as part of the decentralisation process, when the government abolished the previous <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Chad" title="Prefectures of Chad">14 prefectures</a>. Each region is headed by a presidentially appointed governor. Prefects administer the <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Chad" title="Departments of Chad">61 departments</a> within the regions.<sup id="cite_ref-circonscritions_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circonscritions-95">[95]</a></sup> The departments are divided into <a href="/wiki/Sub-prefectures_of_Chad" title="Sub-prefectures of Chad">200 sub-prefectures</a>, which are in turn composed of 446 cantons.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The cantons are scheduled to be replaced by <i>communautés rurales</i>, but the legal and regulatory framework has not yet been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-WB1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB1-98">[98]</a></sup> The constitution provides for decentralised government to compel local populations to play an active role in their own development.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> To this end, the constitution declares that each administrative subdivisions be governed by elected local assemblies,<sup id="cite_ref-decentralisation_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-decentralisation-100">[100]</a></sup> but no local elections have taken place,<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-101">[101]</a></sup> and communal elections scheduled for 2005 have been repeatedly postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-HRP_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRP-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Chad" title="Military of Chad">Military of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The CIA World Factbook estimates the military budget of Chad to be 4.2% of GDP as of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Given the then GDP ($7.095 bln) of the country, military spending was estimated to be about $300&nbsp;million. This estimate however dropped after the end of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_war_in_Chad_(2005%E2%80%932010)" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil war in Chad (2005–2010)">Civil war in Chad (2005–2010)</a> to 2.0%<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> as estimated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> for the year 2011. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Chad" title="Economy of Chad">Economy of Chad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Chad" title="Agriculture in Chad">Agriculture in Chad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Chad" title="Petroleum industry in Chad">Petroleum industry in Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg" decoding="async" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="865"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Chad.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Chad's product exports in 28 color-coded categories.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> ranks Chad as the seventh poorest country in the world, with 80% of the population living below the poverty line. The <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>) per capita was estimated as <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1,651 in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-5">[5]</a></sup> Chad is part of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Central_African_States" title="Bank of Central African States">Bank of Central African States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Customs_and_Economic_Union_of_Central_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Customs and Economic Union of Central Africa">Customs and Economic Union of Central Africa</a> (UDEAC) and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chad's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_CFA_franc" title="Central African CFA franc">CFA franc</a>. In the 1960s, the <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Chad" title="Mining industry of Chad">mining industry of Chad</a> produced <a href="/wiki/Sodium_carbonate" title="Sodium carbonate">sodium carbonate</a>, or natron. There have also been reports of <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>-bearing quartz in the <a href="/wiki/Biltine_Prefecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Biltine Prefecture">Biltine Prefecture</a>. However, years of civil war have scared away foreign investors; those who left Chad between 1979 and 1982 have only recently begun to regain confidence in the country's future. In 2000 major direct foreign investment in the oil sector began, boosting the country's economic prospects.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mao_Women.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mao_Women.jpg/220px-Mao_Women.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mao_Women.jpg/330px-Mao_Women.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mao_Women.jpg/440px-Mao_Women.jpg 2x" data-file-width="477" data-file-height="318"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mao_Women.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Women in <a href="/wiki/Mao,_Chad" title="Mao, Chad">Mao</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Utilities_in_Chad" title="Utilities in Chad">water</a> is provided by a water tower. Access to clean water is often a problem in Chad.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>An uneven inclusion into the global political economy as a site for colonial resource extraction (primarily cotton and crude oil), a global economic system that does not promote nor encourage the development of Chadian industrialization,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and the failure to support local agricultural production has meant that the majority of Chadians live in daily uncertainty and hunger.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Over 80% of Chad's population relies on subsistence farming and livestock raising for its livelihood.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-38">[38]</a></sup> The crops grown and the locations of herds are determined by the local climate. In the southernmost 10% of the territory lies the nation's most fertile cropland, with rich yields of <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>. In the Sahel only the hardier varieties of millet grow, and these with much lower yields than in the south. On the other hand, the Sahel is ideal pastureland for large herds of commercial cattle and for goats, sheep, donkeys and horses. The Sahara's scattered <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oases</a> support only some dates and legumes.<sup id="cite_ref-Collelo_10-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collelo-10">[10]</a></sup> Chad's cities face serious difficulties of municipal infrastructure; only 48% of urban residents have access to potable water and only 2% to basic sanitation.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WB1_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB1-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before the development of oil industry, cotton dominated industry and the labour market accounted for approximately 80% of export earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Cotton remains a primary export, although exact figures are not available. Rehabilitation of <a href="/wiki/Cotontchad" title="Cotontchad">Cotontchad</a>, a major cotton company weakened by a decline in world cotton prices, has been financed by France, the Netherlands, the European Union, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a> (IBRD). The <a href="/wiki/Parastatal" class="mw-redirect" title="Parastatal">parastatal</a> is now expected to be privatised.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup> Other than cotton, <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gum_arabic" title="Gum arabic">gum arabic</a> are dominant.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, Chad has been affected by a <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_crisis" title="Humanitarian crisis">humanitarian crisis</a> since at least 2001. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the country of Chad hosts over 280,000 refugees from the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> region, over 55,000 from the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, as well as over 170,000 <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In February 2008 in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%27Djamena_(2008)" title="Battle of N'Djamena (2008)">Battle of N'Djamena</a>, UN Under-Secretary-General for Humanitarian Affairs <a href="/wiki/John_Holmes_(British_diplomat)" title="John Holmes (British diplomat)">John Holmes</a> expressed "extreme concern" that the crisis would have a negative effect on the ability of humanitarians to deliver life-saving assistance to half a million beneficiaries, most of whom – according to him – heavily rely on humanitarian aid for their survival.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> UN spokesperson <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Giuliano" title="Maurizio Giuliano">Maurizio Giuliano</a> stated to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>: "If we do not manage to provide aid at sufficient levels, the humanitarian crisis might become a humanitarian catastrophe".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In addition, organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a> have suspended activities due to killings of aid workers.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Chad" title="Transport in Chad">Transport in Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg/220px-Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg/330px-Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg/440px-Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rebuilt_bridge_on_Bragoto_River.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A bridge on the <a href="/wiki/Bragoto_River" title="Bragoto River">Bragoto River</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Civil war crippled the development of <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Chad" title="Transport in Chad">transport infrastructure</a>; in 1987, Chad had only 30 kilometres (19&nbsp;mi) of paved roads. Successive road rehabilitation projects improved the network<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> to 550 kilometres (340&nbsp;mi) by 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the road network is limited; roads are often unusable for several months of the year. With no railways of its own, Chad depends heavily on Cameroon's rail system for the transport of Chadian exports and imports to and from the seaport of <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography-116">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg/220px-Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg/330px-Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg/440px-Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="453"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aeroport_abech%C3%A91.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An airplane landing in <a href="/wiki/Ab%C3%A9ch%C3%A9" title="Abéché">Abéché</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Chad" title="List of airports in Chad">List of airports in Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chad&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Chad had an estimated 59 airports, only 9 of which had paved runways.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA-WFB_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-WFB-117">[117]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/N%27Djamena_International_Airport" title="N'Djamena International Airport">international airport</a> serves the capital and provides regular nonstop flights to Paris and several African cities. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Chad" title="Energy in Chad">Energy in Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad's energy sector has had years of mismanagement by the parastatal Chad Water and Electric Society (STEE), which provides power for 15% of the capital's citizens and covers only 1.5% of the national population.<sup id="cite_ref-CCG_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCG-118">[118]</a></sup> Most Chadians burn biomass fuels such as wood and animal manure for power.<sup id="cite_ref-EIA_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-119">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a> leads a consortium of <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petronas" title="Petronas">Petronas</a> that has invested $3.7&nbsp;billion to develop oil reserves estimated at one billion barrels in southern Chad. Oil production began in 2003 with the <a href="/wiki/Chad-Cameroon_Petroleum_Development_and_Pipeline_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Chad-Cameroon Petroleum Development and Pipeline Project">completion of a pipeline</a> (financed in part by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>) that links the southern oilfields to terminals on the Atlantic coast of Cameroon. As a condition of its assistance, the World Bank insisted that 80% of oil revenues be spent on development projects. In January 2006 the World Bank suspended its loan programme when the Chadian government passed laws reducing this amount.<sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OECD_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-101">[101]</a></sup> On 14 July 2006, the World Bank and Chad signed a memorandum of understanding under which the Government of Chad commits 70% of its spending to priority poverty reduction programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Chad" title="Telecommunications in Chad">Telecommunications in Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications in Chad">telecommunication system</a> is basic and expensive, with fixed telephone services provided by the state telephone company <a href="/wiki/SotelTchad" title="SotelTchad">SotelTchad</a>. In 2000, there were only 14 fixed telephone lines per 10,000 inhabitants in the country, one of the lowest telephone densities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CCG_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCG-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Gateway_Communications" title="Gateway Communications">Gateway Communications</a>, a pan-African wholesale connectivity and telecommunications provider also has a presence in Chad.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In September 2013, Chad's Ministry for Posts and Information &amp; Communication Technologies (PNTIC) announced that the country will be seeking a partner for <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">fiber optic</a> technology. </p>
      <p>Chad is ranked last in the World Economic Forum's Network Readiness Index (NRI) – an indicator for determining the development level of a country's information and communication technologies. Chad ranked number 148 out of 148 overall in the 2014 NRI ranking, down from 142 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In September 2010 the mobile phone penetration rate was estimated at 24.3% over a population estimate of 10.7&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-Chad_Mobile_Market_(Q1_2008_-_Q3_2010)_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chad_Mobile_Market_(Q1_2008_-_Q3_2010)-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Chad">Media of Chad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Chad's television audience is limited to N'Djamena. The only television station is the state-owned Télé Tchad. Radio has a far greater reach, with 13 private radio stations.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Newspapers are limited in quantity and distribution, and circulation figures are small due to transportation costs, low literacy rates, and poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EIA_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> While the constitution defends liberty of expression, the government has regularly restricted this right, and at the end of 2006 began to enact a system of prior <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> on the media.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Chad" title="Education in Chad">Educators</a> face considerable challenges due to the nation's dispersed population and a certain degree of reluctance on the part of parents to send their children to school. Although attendance is compulsory, only 68 percent of boys attend primary school, and more than half of the population is illiterate. <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Chad" title="List of universities in Chad">Higher education</a> is provided at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_N%27Djamena" title="University of N'Djamena">University of N'Djamena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BGN_68-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGN-68">[68]</a></sup> At 33 percent, Chad has one of the lowest literacy rates of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Labor" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Labor">U.S. Department of Labor</a>'s Findings on the Worst Forms of Child Labor<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> in Chad reported that school attendance of children aged 5 to 14 was as low as 39%. This can also be related to the issue of <a href="/wiki/Child_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Child labor">child labor</a> as the report also stated that 53% of children aged 5 to 14 were working children, and that 30% of children aged 7 to 14 combined work and school. A more recent DOL <a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">report</a> listed cattle herding as a major agricultural activity that employed underage children.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin:10px;"> 
       <caption>
        <b>Holidays</b><sup id="cite_ref-CCG_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCG-118">[118]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th style="font-size: smaller;">Date </th> 
         <th style="font-size: smaller;">English Name </th>
        </tr>

         <td>1 January </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1 May </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>25 May </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/African_Liberation_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="African Liberation Day">African Liberation Day</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>11 August </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Independence_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence Day">Independence Day</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1 November </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day" title="All Saints' Day">All Saints' Day</a> </td>
        </tr>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1 December </td>

        </tr>

         <td>25 December </td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Because of its great variety of peoples and languages, Chad possesses a rich cultural heritage. The Chadian government has actively promoted Chadian culture and national traditions by opening the <a href="/wiki/Chad_National_Museum" title="Chad National Museum">Chad National Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chad_Cultural_Centre" title="Chad Cultural Centre">Chad Cultural Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_40-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-40">[40]</a></sup> Six <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Chad" title="Public holidays in Chad">national holidays</a> are observed throughout the year, and movable holidays include the Christian holiday of <a href="/wiki/Easter_Monday" title="Easter Monday">Easter Monday</a> and the Muslim holidays of <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid ul-Fitr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Adha" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Adha">Eid ul-Adha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">Eid Milad Nnabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CCG_118-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCG-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Chad" title="Music of Chad">music of Chad</a> includes a number of instruments such as the <i>kinde</i>, a type of bow harp; the <i><a href="/wiki/Kakaki" title="Kakaki">kakaki</a></i>, a long tin horn; and the <i>hu hu</i>, a stringed instrument that uses <a href="/wiki/Calabash" title="Calabash">calabashes</a> as loudspeakers. Other instruments and their combinations are more linked to specific ethnic groups: the Sara prefer whistles, <a href="/wiki/Balafon" title="Balafon">balafones</a>, harps and <i>kodjo</i> drums; and the <a href="/wiki/Kanembu_people" title="Kanembu people">Kanembu</a> combine the sounds of drums with those of flute-like instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-132">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tailor_in_Chad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Tailor_in_Chad.jpg/220px-Tailor_in_Chad.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Tailor_in_Chad.jpg/330px-Tailor_in_Chad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Tailor_in_Chad.jpg/440px-Tailor_in_Chad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tailor_in_Chad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Chadian tailor sells traditional dresses.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">Millet</a> is the staple food of <a href="/wiki/Chadian_cuisine" title="Chadian cuisine">Chadian cuisine</a>. It is used to make balls of paste that are dipped in sauces. In the north this dish is known as <i>alysh</i>; in the south, as <i>biya</i>. Fish is popular, which is generally prepared and sold either as <i>salanga</i> (sun-dried and lightly smoked <i><a href="/wiki/Alestes" title="Alestes">Alestes</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hydrocynus" title="Hydrocynus">Hydrocynus</a></i>) or as <i>banda</i> (smoked large fish).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> <i>Carcaje</i> is a popular sweet red tea extracted from hibiscus leaves. Alcoholic beverages, though absent in the north, are popular in the south, where people drink <a href="/wiki/Millet_beer" title="Millet beer">millet beer</a>, known as <i>billi-billi</i> when brewed from red millet, and as <i>coshate</i> when from <a href="/wiki/Proso_millet" title="Proso millet">white millet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-132">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The music group <a href="/wiki/Chari_Jazz" title="Chari Jazz">Chari Jazz</a> formed in 1964 and initiated Chad's modern music scene. Later, more renowned groups such as African Melody and International Challal attempted to mix modernity and tradition. Popular groups such as Tibesti have clung faster to their heritage by drawing on <i>sai</i>, a traditional style of music from southern Chad. The people of Chad have customarily disdained modern music. However, in 1995 greater interest has developed and fostered the distribution of CDs and audio cassettes featuring Chadian artists. Piracy and a lack of legal protections for artists' rights remain problems to further development of the Chadian music industry.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg/220px-Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg/330px-Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg/440px-Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Criquets_grill%C3%A9s_ou_fris.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Criquets grillés ou fris
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As in other Sahelian countries, <a href="/wiki/Chadian_literature" title="Chadian literature">literature in Chad</a> has seen an economic, political and spiritual drought that has affected its best known writers. Chadian authors have been forced to write from exile or expatriate status and have generated literature dominated by themes of political oppression and historical discourse. Since 1962, 20 Chadian authors have written some 60 works of fiction. Among the most internationally renowned writers are <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Brahim_Se%C3%AFd" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Brahim Seïd">Joseph Brahim Seïd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baba_Moustapha" title="Baba Moustapha">Baba Moustapha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Bangui" title="Antoine Bangui">Antoine Bangui</a> and <a href="/wiki/Koulsy_Lamko" title="Koulsy Lamko">Koulsy Lamko</a>. In 2003 Chad's sole literary critic, <a href="/wiki/Ahmat_Taboye" title="Ahmat Taboye">Ahmat Taboye</a>, published his <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Anthologie de la littérature tchadienne</i> to further knowledge of Chad's literature internationally and among youth and to make up for Chad's lack of publishing houses and promotional structure.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_132-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The development of a <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Chad" title="Cinema of Chad">Chadian film</a> industry, which began with the short films of <a href="/wiki/Edouard_Sailly" title="Edouard Sailly">Edouard Sailly</a> in the 1960s, was hampered by the devastations of civil wars and from the lack of <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">cinemas</a>, of which there is currently only one in the whole country (the <i>Normandie</i> in N'Djamena).<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The Chadian <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">feature film</a> industry began growing again in the 1990s, with the work of directors <a href="/wiki/Mahamat-Saleh_Haroun" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahamat-Saleh Haroun">Mahamat-Saleh Haroun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Issa_Serge_Coelo" title="Issa Serge Coelo">Issa Serge Coelo</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Abakar_Chene_Massar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abakar Chene Massar (page does not exist)">Abakar Chene Massar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Haroun's film <i><a href="/wiki/Abouna_(film)" title="Abouna (film)">Abouna</a></i> was critically acclaimed, and his <i><a href="/wiki/Daratt" title="Daratt">Daratt</a></i> won the Grand Special Jury Prize at the <a href="/wiki/63rd_Venice_International_Film_Festival" title="63rd Venice International Film Festival">63rd Venice International Film Festival</a>. The 2010 feature film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Screaming_Man" title="A Screaming Man">A Screaming Man</a></i> won the <a href="/wiki/Jury_Prize_(Cannes_Film_Festival)" title="Jury Prize (Cannes Film Festival)">Jury Prize</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2010 Cannes Film Festival">2010 Cannes Film Festival</a>, making Haroun the first Chadian director to enter, as well as win, an award in the main Cannes competition.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Issa_Serge_Coelo" title="Issa Serge Coelo">Issa Serge Coelo</a> directed the films, <i><a href="/wiki/Daresalam" title="Daresalam">Daresalam</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/DP75:_Tartina_City" title="DP75: Tartina City">DP75: Tartina City</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is Chad's most popular <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Chad" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport in Chad">sport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Chad_national_football_team" title="Chad national football team">national team</a> is closely followed during international competitions<sup id="cite_ref-culture_132-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-132">[132]</a></sup> and Chadian footballers have played for French teams. <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_wrestling" title="Freestyle wrestling">freestyle wrestling</a> are widely practiced, the latter in a form in which the wrestlers put on traditional animal hides and cover themselves with dust.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_132-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-132">[132]</a></sup> </p>
